## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting stress (sigma) from strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in solid mechanics and materials science. The relationship captures how materials deform under load at different temperatures, involving elastic moduli, thermal softening, strain hardening, and potentially viscoelastic or thermoplastic effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain relationship)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal modulus correction)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic stress-strain curve)
- Thermal softening with power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal term)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (modulus with Arrhenius-type temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Thermal polynomial: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature-dependent modulus)
- Hyperbolic sine creep: sigma = c0 * (sinh(c1 * epsilon))**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (high-temperature deformation with sinh flow rule)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain at small strains transitioning to nonlinear at large strains → piecewise or power-law with exponent < 1
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiplicative factor on strain term that decreases with T, e.g., (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c0/T)
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon))
- Yield stress offset → additive constant: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon), indicating initial yield before hardening
- Thermal softening at high temperatures → multiplicative term (1 - c0*T**c1) or exp(-c0*T) reducing stress magnitude
- Strain-temperature coupling → product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c0 * T**c1 indicating thermomechanical interaction
- Phase transition or abrupt modulus change → sigmoidal function of T multiplying strain terms, e.g., 1/(1+exp(c0*(T-c1)))
- Creep/viscoplastic behavior at high T → sinh or exponential functions of stress/strain with Arrhenius temperature terms
